Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Mines and Mining
=================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 1 - Mining Claims
**********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-1 Lode claims -- Size and shape -- Discovery necessary.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A lode mining claim, whether located by one or more persons, may equal, but shall not exceed, 1,500 feet in length along the vein or lode and may extend 300 feet on each side of the middle of the vein at the surface, except where adverse rights render a lesser width necessary. The end lines of each claim must be parallel. No location of a mining claim shall be made until the discovery of the vein or lode within the limits of the claim located.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2 Discovery monument -- Notice of location -- Contents.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The locator at the time of making the discovery of such vein or lode must erect a monument at the place of discovery, and post thereon his notice of location which shall contain:Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2(1): The name of the claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2(2): The name of the locator or locators.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2(3): The date of the location.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2(4): If a lode claim, the number of linear feet claimed in length along the course of the vein each way from the point of discovery, with the width claimed on each side of the center of the vein, and the general course of the vein or lode as near as may be, and such a description of the claim, located by reference to some natural object or permanent monument, as will identify the claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-2(5): If a placer or mill site claim, the number of acres or superficial feet claimed, and such a description of the claim or mill site, located by reference to some natural object or permanent monument, as will identify the claim or mill site.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-3 Boundaries to be marked.
-----------------------------------------------------
Mining claims and mill sites must be distinctly marked on the ground so that the boundaries thereof can be readily traced.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-4 Copy of location notice to be recorded.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Within 30 days after the date of posting the location notice upon the claim, the locator, or the locator's assigns, shall record a substantial copy of the notice of location in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the claim is situated.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6 Affidavit of performance of annual labor or payment of maintenance fee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(1): As used in this section, "assessment work" means the performance of labor or making of improvements on or for the benefit of a mining claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(2): Within 30 days after the end of the annual period specified in 30 U.S.C. Sec. 28 the owner of an unpatented lode or placer mining claim,  or a mill or tunnel site claim or someone  on his behalf, shall record an affidavit in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the claim is located setting forth:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(2)(a): the name and address of the owner of the claim;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(2)(b): the name of the claim and the serial number, if any, assigned to the claim by the United States Bureau of Land Management;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(2)(c): if assessment work was required to be performed under 30 U.S.C. Sec. 28 or other federal law to maintain the claim, a statement that the annual assessment work required  to maintain the claim was performed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(2)(d): if the assessment work was not required to be performed under 30 U.S.C. Sec. 28 or other federal law, a statement that it is the intention of the owner to hold the claim, and if a claim maintenance fee was paid as required by the Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1993, Pub. L. 103-66 or other federal law, a statement that the fee was paid in a timely manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(3): The affidavit, or a certified copy, shall be prima facie evidence of the facts stated in the affidavit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-6(4): The amendments made in this section do not affect any act or right accruing or which has accrued or been established or any suit or proceeding commenced before May 1, 1995.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-7 District recorders -- Office abolished.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
From and after the termination of the office of any mining district recorder now holding office in this state such district shall be abolished and such office shall become vacant.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-8 Vacancy and removal -- County recorder to receive records.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-8(1): If there is a vacancy in the office of recorder of any mining district, or if there is no person in the mining district authorized to retain the custody and give certified copies of the records, the person having custody of the records shall deposit them in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the mining district, or the greater part of the mining district, is situated.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-8(2): That county recorder shall take possession of the records and may make and certify copies from the records, including any other copies of records and papers in the recorder's office pertaining to mining claims.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-8(3): Those certified copies shall be receivable in evidence in all courts and before all officers and tribunals.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-8(4): The production of a certified copy shall be, without further proof, evidence that the records were properly in the custody of the county recorder.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-9 County recorder may certify district records.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-9(1): When the books, records, and documents pertaining to the office of mining district recorder have been deposited in the office of a county recorder, the recorder may make and certify copies from those records.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-9(2): Those certified copies shall be receivable in all tribunals and before all officers of this state in the same manner and to the same effect as if the records had been originally filed or made in the office of the county recorder.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-10 Certified copies of records evidence.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Copies of notices of location of mining claims, mill sites and tunnel sites heretofore recorded in the records of the several mining districts, and copies of the mining rules and regulations in force therein and recorded, when duly certified by the district or county recorder, shall be receivable in all tribunals and before all officers of this state as prima facie evidence.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-11 Interfering with notices, stakes, or monuments -- Penalty.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any person who intentionally or knowingly tears down or defaces a notice posted on a mining claim, or takes up or destroys any stake or monument marking the claim, or interferes with any person lawfully in possession of the claim, or who alters, erases, defaces, or destroys any record kept by a mining district or county recorder, is guilty of a class B misdemeanor, and shall be punished by a fine of not less than $25 nor more than $100, or by imprisonment for not less than 10 days nor more than six months, or by both the fine and imprisonment.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-1-12 Damages for wrongful removal of ores.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
When damages are claimed for the extraction or selling of ore from any mine or mining claim and the defendant, or those under whom he claims, holds, under color of title adverse to the claims of the plaintiff, in good faith, then the reasonable value of all labor bestowed or expenses incurred in necessary developing, mining, transporting, concentrating, selling or preparing said ore, or its mineral content, for market, must be allowed as an offset against such damages; provided, however, that any person who, wrongfully entering upon any mine or mining claim and carrying away ores therefrom, or wrongfully extracting and selling ores from any mine, having knowledge of the existence of adverse claimants in any mine or mining claim, and without notice to them, knowingly and willfully trespasses in or upon such mine or mining claim and extracts or sells ore therefrom shall be liable to the owners of such ore for three times the value thereof without any deductions either for labor bestowed or expenses incurred in removing, transporting, selling or preparing said ore, or its mineral content for market.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 2 - Coal Mine Safety Act
*****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Coal Mine Safety Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1): "Adverse action" means to take any of the following actions against a person in a manner that affects the person's employment or contractual relationships:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(a): discharge the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(b): threaten the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(c): coerce the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(d): intimidate the person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e): discriminate against the person, including to discriminate in:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(i): compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(ii): terms;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(iii): conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(iv): location;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(v): rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(vi): immunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(vii): promotions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(1)(e)(viii): privileges.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2): "Coal mine" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a): the following used in extracting coal from its natural deposits in the earth by any means or method:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(i): the land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(ii): a structure;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(iii): a facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(iv): machinery;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(v): a tool;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(vi): equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(vii): a shaft;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(viii): a slope;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(ix): a tunnel;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(x): an excavation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(a)(xi): other property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(2)(b): the work of preparing extracted coal, including a coal preparation facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(3): 34A-1-103 "Commission" means the Labor Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(4): 34A-1-201 "Commissioner" means the commissioner appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(5): 40-2-203 "Council" means the Mine Safety Technical Advisory Council created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(6): 40-2-202 "Director" means the director of the Utah Office of Coal Mine Safety appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7): "Major coal mine accident" means any of the following at a coal mine located in Utah:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7)(a): a mine explosion;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7)(b): a mine fire;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7)(c): the flooding of a mine;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7)(d): a mine collapse; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(7)(e): the accidental death of an individual at a mine.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(8): "Mine Safety and Health Administration" means the federal Mine Safety and Health Administration within the United States Department of Labor.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(9): 40-2-201 "Office" means the Utah Office of Coal Mine Safety created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(10): 40-2-204 "Panel" means the Coal Miner Certification Panel created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-102(11): "Unsafe condition" means a danger that reasonably could be expected to cause serious harm to a person or property.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-103 Scope and administration of chapter.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-103(1): This chapter applies to any coal mine located in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-103(2): The commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-103(2)(a): shall administer this chapter with the assistance of the office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-103(2)(b): has jurisdiction over a coal mine in this state as set forth in this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-104 Rulemaking authority.
----------------------------------------------------
In accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-201 Utah Office of Coal Mine Safety created.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-201(1): There is created within the commission the "Utah Office of Coal Mine Safety."
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-201(2): The office, under the direction of the commissioner, shall assist the commission in administering this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202 Appointment of director.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(1): The director is the chief officer of the office and serves as the executive and administrative head of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(2)(a): The commissioner shall appoint the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(2)(b): The director may be removed from that position at the will of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(3): Title 63A, Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act The director shall receive compensation as provided by
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-202(4): The director shall be experienced in administration and possess such additional qualifications as determined by the commissioner.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203 Mine Safety Technical Advisory Council created -- Duties.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(1): Within the office there is created the "Mine Safety Technical Advisory Council" consisting of 13 voting members and five nonvoting members as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a): The commissioner shall appoint the voting members of the council as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(i): one individual who represents a coal miner union;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(ii): two individuals with coal mining experience;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(iii): two individuals who represent coal mine operators;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(iv): one individual who represents an industry trade association;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(v): two individuals from local law enforcement agencies or emergency medical service providers;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vi): three individuals who have expertise in one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vi)(A): seismology;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vi)(B): mining engineering;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vi)(C): mine safety; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vi)(D): another related subject; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(a)(vii): two individuals from entities that provide mine safety training.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b): The nonvoting members of the council are:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b)(i): the commissioner or the commissioner's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b)(ii): the executive director of the Department of Natural Resources or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b)(iii): the commissioner of the Department of Public Safety or the commissioner's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b)(iv): a representative of the Mine Safety and Health Administration selected by the Mine Safety and Health Administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(2)(b)(v): a representative of the federal Bureau of Land Management selected by the federal Bureau of Land Management.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(4)(a): The commissioner shall terminate the term of a voting member who ceases to be representative as designated by the voting member's original appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(4)(b): If a vacancy occurs in the voting members, the commissioner shall appoint a replacement for the unexpired term after soliciting recommendations from the council members.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(5)(a): The council shall meet at least quarterly.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(8)(a): safety of coal mines located in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-203(8)(b): prevention of coal mine accidents;

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(1)(a): direct the state's efforts to promote coal mine safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(1)(b): participate with the Mine Safety and Health Administration in an investigation of a major coal mine accident in Utah.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(2)(a): 40-2-302 a system consistent with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(3)(a): conduct one or more studies to promote coal mine safety;

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(3)(d): serve as the lead state agency in developing and implementing state and local response and communication plans for major coal mine accidents in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-301(3)(e): (2)(b) implement the notification requirements established under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302 Reporting of an unsafe condition in coal mines -- Adverse action prohibited.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1): Subject to the other provisions of this section, upon the office's receipt of information from a person of a possible unsafe condition in a coal mine located in Utah, the office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1)(a): notify the federal Mine Safety and Health Administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1)(b): notify another appropriate federal, state, or local government agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1)(c): contact the operator of the coal mine;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1)(d): refer the information to the council on a confidential basis; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(1)(e): take any other authorized action.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(2): The commission, council, or office may not disclose or otherwise make public the identity of a person who reports a possible unsafe condition in a coal mine located in Utah unless that person authorizes the commission, council, or office to disclose the person's identity.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(3): A coal mine operator may not take adverse action against a person because that person:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(3)(a): reports an alleged unsafe mine condition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-302(3)(b): testifies, assists, or participates in any manner in an investigation, proceeding, or hearing under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303 Annual report on coal mine safety.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(1): By October 1 of each year, the commission, office, and council shall compile and submit to the governor and the Legislature a comprehensive report of the status of coal mine safety within the state for the immediately preceding calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2): The report required by this section shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2)(a): a compilation of major coal mine accidents or other coal mine emergencies within the state during the calendar year;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2)(b): a statement of actions by the commission, office, or council to implement this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2)(c): without a breach in confidentiality, a summary of reports of alleged unsafe conditions received by the office, with a statement of the office's responses;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2)(d): recommendations for additional action to promote coal mine safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-303(2)(e): any other items the commission, office, and council consider appropriate.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402 Certification requirements.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(1): The commission shall collect a fee for:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(1)(a): the taking of a certification test; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(1)(b): the retaking of one or more sections of a certification test.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(4)(c)(ii): six months' experience may be credited to a graduate of a two-year course in mining technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(4)(d): An applicant who wishes to obtain an underground mine electrician certificate shall have at least one year of varied electrical experience as specified in 30 C.F.R. Sec. 75.153.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-2-402(4)(e): An applicant who wishes to obtain a surface mine electrician certificate shall have at least one year of varied surface electrical experience as specified in 30 C.F.R. Sec. 77.103.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 5 - Miscellaneous Safety Provisions
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-5-6 Mine rescue team required -- Immunity of rescue participants.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-5-6(1): Each mine owner shall maintain and support a mine rescue team at such owner's mine or otherwise ensure the availability of a mine rescue team in the event of an emergency, in accordance with the requirements of the Federal Mine Safety and Health Act of 1977, and the regulations promulgated under it.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-5-6(2): An individual, mine owner, or sponsoring owner who participates in a mine rescue operation during an emergency at the owner or sponsor's mine and who in good faith provides emergency care or assistance to an injured person during the emergency, is not liable in damages to such injured person on account of rendering emergency care or assistance.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 6 - Board and Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining
***************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-1 Declaration of public interest.
------------------------------------------------------------
It is declared to be in the public interest to foster, encourage, and  promote the development, production, and utilization of natural resources of oil and gas in the state of Utah in such a manner as will prevent waste; to authorize and to provide for the operation and development of oil and gas properties in such a manner that a greater ultimate recovery of oil and gas may be obtained and that the correlative rights of all owners may be fully protected; to provide exclusive state authority over oil and gas exploration and development as regulated under the provisions of this chapter; to encourage, authorize, and provide for voluntary agreements for cycling, recycling, pressure maintenance, and secondary recovery operations in order that the greatest possible economic recovery of oil and gas may be obtained within the state to the end that the land owners, the royalty owners, the producers, and the general public may realize and enjoy the greatest possible good from these vital natural resources.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2 Definitions.
-----------------------------------------
For the purpose of this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(1): "Board" means the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(2): "Correlative rights" means the opportunity of each owner in a pool to produce the owner's just and equitable share of the oil and gas in the pool without waste.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(3): "Condensate" means hydrocarbons, regardless of gravity, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(3)(a): occur naturally in the gaseous phase in the reservoir; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(3)(b): are separated from the natural gas as liquids through the process of condensation either in the reservoir, in the wellbore, or at the surface in field separators.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(4): "Consenting owner" means an owner who, in the manner and within the time frame established by the board in rule, consents to the drilling and operation of a well and agrees to bear the owner's proportionate share of the costs of the drilling and operation of the well.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(5): 40-6-5(3)(c) "Crude oil" means hydrocarbons, regardless of gravity, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(5)(a): are produced at the wellhead in liquid form; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(5)(b): 40-6-5(3)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(5)(b)(i): occur naturally in the liquid phase in the reservoir; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(5)(b)(ii): 40-6-5(3)(c) are produced through enhanced recovery operations authorized by the board in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(6): "Division" means the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(7): (10); (11); (17)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(7)(a): (10); (11); (17) "Gas" means natural gas, as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(7)(b): "Gas" does not include any gaseous or liquid substance processed from coal, oil shale, or tar sands.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(8): "Illegal oil" or "illegal gas" means oil or gas that has been produced from any well within the state in violation of this chapter or any rule or order of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(9): "Illegal product" means any product derived in whole or in part from illegal oil or illegal gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(10): (11); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(10)(a): (11); (3) "Natural gas" means hydrocarbons that occur naturally in the gaseous phase in the reservoir and are produced and recovered at the wellhead in gaseous form, except natural gas liquids as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(10)(b): "Natural gas" includes coalbed methane gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(11): "Natural gas liquids" means hydrocarbons, regardless of gravity, that are separated from  natural gas as liquids in gas processing plants through the process of condensation, absorption, adsorption, or other methods.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(12): "Nonconsenting owner" means an owner who does not, after written notice and in the manner and within the time frame established by the board in rule, consent to the drilling and operation of a well or agree to bear the owner's proportionate share of the costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(13): (5); (3); (13)(c); 40-6-5(3)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(13)(a): (5); (3) "Oil" means crude oil, as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(13)(b): (13)(c) "Oil" does not include, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(13)(c): 40-6-5(3)(c) "Oil" includes tar sands produced at the wellhead in liquid form through enhanced recovery operations authorized by the board in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(14): "Oil and gas operations" means to explore for, develop, or produce oil and gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a): "Oil and gas proceeds" means any payment that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a)(i): derives from oil and gas production from any well located in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a)(ii): is expressed as a right to a specified interest in the:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a)(ii)(A): cash proceeds received from the sale of the oil and gas; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a)(ii)(B): the cash value of the oil and gas; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(a)(iii): is subject to any tax withheld from the payment pursuant to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(b): "Oil and gas proceeds" includes a royalty interest, overriding royalty interest, production payment interest, or working interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(c): "Oil and gas proceeds" does not include a net profits interest or other interest the extent of which cannot be determined with reference to a specified share of:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(c)(i): the cash proceeds received from the sale of the oil and gas; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(15)(c)(ii): the cash value of the oil and gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(16): "Operator" means a person who has been designated by the owners or the board to operate a well or unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(17): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(17)(a): "Other gas" means nonhydrocarbon gases that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(17)(a)(i): occur naturally in the gaseous phase in the reservoir; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(17)(a)(ii): are injected into the reservoir in connection with pressure maintenance, gas cycling, or other secondary or enhanced recovery projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(17)(b): "Other gas" includes hydrogen sulfide, carbon dioxide, helium, and nitrogen.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(18): "Owner" means a person who has the right:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(18)(a): to drill into and produce from a reservoir; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(18)(b): to appropriate the oil and gas produced for that person or for that person and others.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(19): "Payor" means the person who undertakes to distribute oil and gas proceeds to the persons entitled to them, whether as the first purchaser of that production, as operator of the well from which the production was obtained, or as lessee under the lease on which royalty is due.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(20): 68-3-12.5 "Person" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(21): "Pool" means an underground reservoir containing a common accumulation of oil or gas or both.  Each zone of a general structure that is completely separated from any other zone in the structure is a separate pool.  "Common source of supply" and "reservoir" are synonymous with "pool."
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(22): "Pooling" means the bringing together of separately owned interests for the common development and operation of a drilling unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23)(a): "Pore space" means subsurface porous material possessing free space, naturally or artificially created, between the mineral grains.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23)(b): "Pore space":
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23)(b)(i): is expressed as a percentage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23)(b)(ii): depends on the size and sorting of the subsurface material's particles as a cubic or hexagonic package.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(23)(c): "Pore space" does not include void or cavern space created by the removal of minerals in the course of solution mining or other mining operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(24): "Producer" means the owner or operator of a well capable of producing oil and gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(25): "Product" means any commodity made from oil and gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(26): "Surface land" means privately owned land:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(26)(a): overlying privately owned oil and gas resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(26)(b): upon which oil and gas operations are conducted; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(26)(c): owned by a surface land owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(27): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(27)(a): "Surface land owner" means a person who owns, in fee simple absolute, all or part of the surface land as shown by the records of the county where the surface land is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(27)(b): "Surface land owner" does not include the surface land owner's lessee, renter, tenant, or other contractually related person.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(28): "Surface land owner's property" means a surface land owner's:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(28)(a): surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(28)(b): crops on the surface land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(28)(c): existing improvements on the surface land.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29): "Surface use agreement" means an agreement between an owner or operator and a surface land owner addressing:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29)(a): the use and reclamation of surface land owned by the surface land owner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29)(b): compensation for damage to the surface land caused by oil and gas operations that result in:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29)(b)(i): loss of the surface land owner's crops on the surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29)(b)(ii): loss of value of existing improvements owned by the surface land owner on the surface land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(29)(b)(iii): permanent damage to the surface land.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30): "Waste" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(a): the inefficient, excessive, or improper use or the unnecessary dissipation of oil or gas or reservoir energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(b): the inefficient storing of oil or gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(c): the locating, drilling, equipping, operating, or producing of any oil or gas well in a manner that causes:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(c)(i): a reduction in the quantity of oil or gas ultimately recoverable from a reservoir under prudent and economical operations;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(c)(ii): unnecessary wells to be drilled; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(c)(iii): the loss or destruction of oil or gas either at the surface or subsurface; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(d): the production of oil or gas in excess of:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(d)(i): transportation or storage facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2(30)(d)(ii): the amount reasonably required to be produced as a result of the proper drilling, completing, testing, or operating of a well or otherwise utilized on the lease from which it is produced.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5 Preemption.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1): Title 40, Chapter 6, Board and Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a): Title 40, Chapter 6, Board and Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining As used in this section, "oil and gas activity" means activity associated with the exploration, development, production, processing, and transportation of oil and gas as set forth in
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(i): drilling;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(ii): hydraulic fracture stimulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(iii): completion, maintenance, reworking, recompletion, disposal, plugging, and abandonment of wells;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(iv): construction activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(v): secondary and tertiary recovery techniques;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(vi): remediation activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(a)(vii): any other activity identified by the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(1)(b): Oil and gas activity does not include any activity or authority directly authorized or granted to a political subdivision by the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(2): Subject to relevant federal law, regulation of oil and gas activity is of statewide concern and the state regulation of oil and gas activity occupies the whole field of potential regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(3): The legislative body of a political subdivision may enact, amend, or enforce a local ordinance, resolution, or rule consistent with its general land use authority that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(3)(a): regulates only surface activity that is incident to an oil and gas activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(3)(b): does not effectively or unduly limit, ban, or prohibit an oil and gas activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-2.5(3)(c): is not otherwise preempted by state or federal law.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5 Jurisdiction of board -- Rules.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The board has jurisdiction over all persons and property necessary to enforce this chapter.  The board shall make rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2): Title 73, Chapter 3, Appropriation; (2)(e); (9); (8); (2)(i); 40-6-11 The board shall make rules and orders as necessary to administer the following provisions:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(a): Ownership of all facilities for the production, storage, treatment, transportation, refining, or processing of oil and gas shall be identified.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(b): Well logs, directional surveys, and reports on well location, drilling, and production shall be made and filed with the division.  Logs of wells marked "confidential" shall be kept confidential for one year after the date on which the log is required to be filed, unless the operator gives written permission to release the log at an earlier date.  Production reports shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(b)(i): filed monthly;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(b)(ii): accurate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(b)(iii): in a form that reasonably serves the needs of state agencies and private fee owners.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(c): Monthly reports from gas processing plants shall be filed with the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d): Wells shall be drilled, cased, cemented, operated, and plugged in such manner as to prevent:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(i): the escape of oil, gas, or water out of the reservoir in which they are found into another formation;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(ii): the detrimental intrusion of water into an oil or gas reservoir;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(iii): the pollution of fresh water supplies by oil, gas, or salt water;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(iv): blowouts;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(v): cavings;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(vi): seepages;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(vii): fires; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(viii): unreasonable:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(viii)(A): loss of a surface land owner's crops on surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(viii)(B): loss of value of existing improvements owned by a surface land owner on surface land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(d)(viii)(C): permanent damage to surface land.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(e): Title 73, Chapter 3, Appropriation; (2)(e) The drilling of wells may not commence without an adequate and approved supply of water as required by
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f): (9); (8) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(i): plug each dry or abandoned well;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(ii): repair each well causing waste or pollution;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(iii): maintain and restore the well site; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(iv): (8) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(iv)(A): loss of a surface land owner's crops on surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(iv)(B): loss of value of existing improvements owned by a surface land owner on surface land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(f)(iv)(C): permanent damage to surface land.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(g): Production from wells shall be separated into oil and gas and measured by means and upon standards that are prescribed by the board and reflect current industry standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(h): Crude oil obtained from any reserve pit, disposal pond or pit, or similar facility, and any accumulation of nonmerchantable waste crude oil shall be treated and processed, as prescribed by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(i): (2)(i) Any person who produces, sells, purchases, acquires, stores, transports, refines, or processes oil or gas or injects fluids for cycling, pressure maintenance, secondary or enhanced recovery, or salt water disposal in this state shall maintain complete and accurate records of the quantities produced, sold, purchased, acquired, stored, transported, refined, processed, or injected for a period of at least six years.  The records shall be available for examination by the board or the board's agents at any reasonable time.  Rules enacted to administer this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-5(2)(j): Any person with an interest in a lease shall be notified when all or part of that interest in the lease is sold or transferred.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6 Drilling units -- Establishment by board -- Modifications -- Prohibitions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(1): The board may order the establishment of drilling units for a pool.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(2): (6); (7) Within each drilling unit, only one well may be drilled for production from the common source of supply, except as provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(3): A drilling unit may not be smaller than the maximum area that can be efficiently and economically drained by one well.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(4)(a): Each drilling unit within a pool shall be of uniform size and shape, unless the board finds that it must make an exception due to geologic, geographic, or other factors.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(4)(b): If the board finds it necessary to divide a pool into zones and establish drilling units for each zone, drilling units may differ in size and shape for each zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(5): An order of the board that establishes drilling units for a pool shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(5)(a): be made upon terms and conditions that are just and reasonable;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(5)(b): include all lands determined by the board to overlay the pool;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(5)(c): specify the acreage and shape of each drilling unit as determined by the board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(5)(d): specify the location of the well in terms of distance from drilling unit boundaries and other wells.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(6): The board may establish a drilling unit and concurrently authorize the drilling of more than one well in a drilling unit if the board finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(6)(a): engineering or geologic characteristics justify the drilling of more than one well in that drilling unit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(6)(b): the drilling of more than one well in the drilling unit will not result in waste.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(7): The board may modify an order that establishes drilling units for a pool to provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(7)(a): an exception to the authorized location of a well;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(7)(b): the inclusion of additional areas which the board determines overlays the pool;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(7)(c): the increase or decrease of the size of drilling units; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(7)(d): the drilling of additional wells within drilling units.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(8)(a): An order of the board that establishes a drilling unit may be made effective retroactively to the date of first production of an existing well located within the drilling unit if no party to the board's proceeding objects to the retroactive application.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(8)(b): An order made retroactive under this section is binding upon a party owning an interest in the drilling unit who receives proper notice of the board's proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(9)(a): After an order establishing drilling units has been entered by the board, the drilling of a well into the pool at a location other than that authorized by the order is prohibited.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6(9)(b): The operation of a well drilled in violation of an order fixing drilling units is prohibited.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5 Pooling of interests for the development and operation of a drilling unit -- Board may order pooling of interests -- Payment of costs and royalty interests -- Monthly accounting.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(1): Two or more owners within a drilling unit may bring together their interests for the development and operation of the drilling unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(a): In the absence of a written agreement for pooling, including a joint operating agreement, the board may enter an order pooling all interests in the drilling unit for the development and operation of the drilling unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(b): The order shall be made upon terms and conditions that are just and reasonable.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(c): The board may adopt terms appearing in a joint operating agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(c)(i): for the drilling unit that is in effect between the consenting owners;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(c)(ii): submitted by any party to the proceeding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(2)(c)(iii): submitted by its own motion.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(3)(a): Operations incident to the drilling of a well upon any portion of a drilling unit covered by a pooling order shall be deemed for all purposes to be the conduct of the operations upon each separately owned tract in the drilling unit by the several owners.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(3)(b): The portion of the production allocated or applicable to a separately owned tract included in a drilling unit covered by a pooling order shall, when produced, be deemed for all purposes to have been produced from that tract by a well drilled on it.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4): (4)(d); (4)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a)(i): Each pooling order shall provide for the payment of just and reasonable costs incurred in the drilling and operating of the drilling unit, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a)(i)(A): the costs of drilling, completing, equipping, producing, gathering, transporting, processing, marketing, and storage facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a)(i)(B): reasonable charges for the administration and supervision of operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a)(i)(C): other costs customarily incurred in the industry.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(a)(ii): An owner is not liable under a pooling order for costs or losses resulting from the gross negligence or willful misconduct of the operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(b): Each pooling order shall provide for reimbursement to the consenting owners for any nonconsenting owner's share of the costs out of production from the drilling unit attributable to the nonconsenting owner's tract.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(c): (4)(d) Each pooling order shall provide that each consenting owner shall own and be entitled to receive, subject to royalty or similar obligations:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(c)(i): the share of the production of the well applicable to the consenting owner's interest in the drilling unit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(c)(ii): (4)(d) unless the consenting owner has agreed otherwise, the consenting owner's proportionate part of the nonconsenting owner's share of the production until costs are recovered as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d): (4)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(i): Each pooling order shall provide that each nonconsenting owner shall be entitled to receive, subject to royalty or similar obligations, the share of the production of the well applicable to the nonconsenting owner's interest in the drilling unit after the consenting owners have recovered from the nonconsenting owner's share of production the following amounts less any cash contributions made by the nonconsenting owner:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(i)(A): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the cost of surface equipment beyond the wellhead connections, including stock tanks, separators, treaters, pumping equipment, and piping;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(i)(B): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the estimated cost to plug and abandon the well as determined by the board;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(i)(C): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the cost of operation of the well commencing with first production and continuing until the consenting owners have recovered all costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(i)(D): an amount to be determined by the board but not less than 150% nor greater than 400% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the costs of staking the location, wellsite preparation, rights-of-way, rigging up, drilling, reworking, recompleting, deepening or plugging back, testing, and completing, and the cost of equipment in the well to and including the wellhead connections.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(ii): (4)(d)(i) The nonconsenting owner's share of the costs specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(d)(iii): A reasonable interest charge may be included if the board finds it appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(4)(e): If there is any dispute about costs, the board shall determine the proper costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(5): If a nonconsenting owner's tract in the drilling unit is subject to a lease or other contract for the development of oil and gas, the pooling order shall provide that the consenting owners shall pay any royalty interest or other interest in the tract not subject to the deduction of the costs of production from the production attributable to that tract.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(6): (4)(d)

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(6)(a)(i): the acreage weighted average landowner's royalty based on each leased fee and privately owned tract within the drilling unit, proportionately reduced by the percentage of the nonconsenting owner's interest in the drilling unit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(6)(a)(ii): if there is no leased fee or privately owned tract within the drilling unit other than the one owned by the nonconsenting owner, 16-2/3% proportionately reduced by the percentage of the nonconsenting owner's interest in the drilling unit.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(8): The operator of a well under a pooling order in which there is a nonconsenting owner shall furnish the nonconsenting owner with monthly statements specifying:

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-6.5(8)(b): the quantity of oil or gas produced; and

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-7 Agreements for repressuring or pressure maintenance or cycling or recycling operations -- Plan for development and operation of pool or field.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-7(1): An agreement for repressuring or pressure maintenance operations, cycling or recycling operations, including the extraction and separation of liquid hydrocarbons from natural gas, or for carrying on any other methods of unit or cooperative development or operation of a field or pool or a part of either, is authorized and may be performed, and shall not be held or construed to violate any statutes relating to trusts, monopolies, or contracts and combinations in restraint of trade, if the agreement is approved by the board as being in the public interest and promotes conservation, increases ultimate recovery and prevents waste of oil or gas provided the agreement protects the correlative rights of each owner or producer.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-7(2): A plan for the development and operation of a pool or field shall be presented to the board and may be approved after notice and hearing.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8 Field or pool units -- Procedure for establishment -- Operation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(1): The board may hold a hearing to consider the need for the operation as a unit of one or more pools or parts of them in a field.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(2): The board shall make an order providing for the unit operation of a pool or part of it, if the board finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(2)(a): Such operation is reasonably necessary for the purposes of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(2)(b): The value of the estimated additional recovery of oil or gas substantially exceeds the estimated additional cost incident to conducting such operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3): Title 38, Chapter 1a, Part 7, Enforcement of Preconstruction and Construction Liens The order shall prescribe a plan for unit operations that shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(a): a description of the lands and of the pool or pools or parts of them to be so operated, termed the unit area;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(b): a statement of the nature of the operations contemplated;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(c): an allocation to the separately owned tracts in the unit area of all the oil and gas that is produced from the unit area and is saved, being the production that is not used in the conduct of operations on the unit area or not unavoidably lost.  The allocation shall be in accord with the agreement, if any, of the interested parties.  If there is no such agreement, the board shall determine the relative value, from evidence introduced at the hearing of the separately owned tracts in the unit area, exclusive of physical equipment, for development of oil and gas by unit operations, and the production allocated to each tract shall be the proportion that the relative value of each tract so determined bears to the relative value of all tracts in the unit area;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(d): a provision for adjustment among the owners of the unit area (not including royalty owners) of their respective investment in wells, tanks, pumps, machinery, materials, equipment, and other things and services of value attributable to the unit operations.  The amount to be charged unit operations for any such item shall be determined by the owners of the unit area (not including royalty owners); but if the owners of the unit area are unable to agree upon the amount or correctness, the board shall determine them.  The net amount charged against the owner of an interest in a separately owned tract shall be considered expense of unit operation chargeable against his interest in the tract.  The adjustments provided for may be treated separately and handled by agreements separate from the unitization agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(e): Title 38, Chapter 1a, Part 7, Enforcement of Preconstruction and Construction Liens a provision providing how the costs of unit operations, including capital investments, shall be determined and charged to the separately owned tracts and how these costs shall be paid, including a provision providing a procedure for the unit production allocated to an owner who does not pay the share of the cost of unit operations charged to such owner, or the interest of such owner, to be sold and the proceeds applied to the payment of such costs.  The operator of the unit shall have a first and prior lien for costs incurred pursuant to the plan of unitization upon each owner's oil and gas rights and his share of unitized production to secure the payment of such owner's proportionate part of the cost of developing and operating the unit area.  This lien may be enforced in the same manner as provided by
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(f): a provision, if necessary, for carrying or otherwise financing any owner who elects to be carried or otherwise financed, allowing a reasonable interest charge for such service payable out of such owner's share of the production;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(g): a provision for the supervision and conduct of the unit operations, in respect to which each owner shall have a percentage vote corresponding to the percentage of the costs of unit operations chargeable against the interest of the owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(h): the time when the unit operations shall commence, and the manner in which, and the circumstances under which, the unit operations shall terminate;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(i): such additional provisions that are found to be appropriate for carrying on the unit operations, and for the protection of correlative rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(3)(j): the designation of a unit operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(4): No order of the board providing for unit operations of a pool or pools shall become effective unless and until the plan for unit operations prescribed by the division has been approved in writing by those owners who, under the board's order, will be required to pay 70% of the costs of the unit operation, and also by the owners of 70% of the production or proceeds that will be credited to interests which are free of cost, such as royalties, overriding royalties, and production payments, and the board has made a finding, either in the order providing for unit operations or in a supplemental order, that the plan for unit operations has been so approved.  If the persons owning required percentage of interest in that unit area do not approve the plan for unit operations within a period of six months from the date on which the order providing for unit operations is made, the order shall be ineffective and shall be revoked by the board unless for good cause shown the board extends this time.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(5): An order providing for unit operations may be amended by an order made by the board in the same manner and subject to the same conditions as an original order providing for unit operations, provided:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(5)(a): If such an amendment affects only the rights and interests of the owners, the approval of the amendment by the owners of royalty, overriding royalty, production payments and other such interests which are free of costs shall not be required.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(5)(b): No such order of amendment shall change the percentage for the allocation of oil and gas as established for any separately owned tract by the original order, or change the percentage for allocation of cost as established for any separately owned tract by the original order.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(6): The board, by an order, may provide for the unit operation of a pool or pools or parts thereof that embrace a unit area established by a previous order of the division.  The order, in providing for the allocation of unit production, shall first treat the unit area previously established as a single tract, and the portion of the unit production allocated shall then be allocated among the separately owned tracts included in the previously established unit area in the same proportions of those specified in the previous order.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(7): An order may provide for unit operations on less than the whole of a pool where the unit area is of such size and shape as may be reasonably required for that purpose, and the conduct will have no adverse effect upon other portions of the pool.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(8): All operations, including, but not limited to, the commencement, drilling, or operation of a well upon any portion of the unit area shall be deemed for all purposes the conduct of such operations upon each separately owned tract in the unit area by the several owners.  The portions of the unit production allocated to a separately owned tract in a unit area shall, when produced, be deemed, for all purposes, to have been actually produced from such tract by a well drilled.  Operations conducted pursuant to an order of the board providing for unit operations shall constitute a fulfillment of all the express or implied obligations for each lease or contract covering lands in the unit area to the extent that compliance with such obligations cannot be had because of the order of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(9): The portion of the unit production allocated to any tract, and the proceeds from the sale, shall be the property and income of the several owners, subject to the rights of royalty owners, to whom, or to whose credit, they are allocated or payable under the order providing for unit operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(10): No division order or other contract relating to the sale or purchase of production from a separately owned tract shall be terminated by the order providing for unit operations but shall remain in force and apply to oil and gas allocated to such tract until terminated in accordance with the provisions thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(11): (3)(e) Except to the extent that the parties affected agree and as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-8(12): 40-6-6 This section shall apply only to field or pool units and shall not apply to the unitization of interests within a drilling unit as may be authorized and governed under the provisions of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9 Proceeds from sale of production -- Payment of proceeds -- Requirements -- Proceeding on petition to determine cause of nonpayment -- Remedies -- Penalties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(1)(a): The oil and gas proceeds derived from the sale of production from any well producing oil or gas in the state shall be paid to any person legally entitled to the payment of the proceeds not later than 180 days after the first day of the month following the date of the first sale and thereafter not later than 30 days after the end of the calendar month within which payment is received by the payor for production, unless other periods or arrangements are provided for in a valid contract with the person entitled to the proceeds.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(1)(b): The payment shall be made directly to the person entitled to the payment by the payor.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(1)(c): The payment is considered to have been made upon deposit in the United States mail.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(2): Payments shall be remitted to any person entitled to oil and gas proceeds annually for the aggregate of up to 12 months accumulation of proceeds, if the total amount owed is $100 or less.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(3): (1); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-9(3)(a): Any delay in determining whether a person is legally entitled to an interest in the oil and gas proceeds does not affect payments to other persons entitled to payment.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(6)(a)(ii): deduct the product taken in-kind; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(6)(a)(iii): pay the levy on the difference.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(6)(b): The interest owner who takes the product in-kind shall file a report and pay the levy on the interest owner's share of production excluded from the operator's report.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(7): This section shall apply to any interest in oil or gas produced in the state except:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(7)(a): any interest of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(7)(b): any interest of the state or a political subdivision of the state in any oil or gas or in the proceeds of the oil or gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(7)(c): any interest of any Indian or Indian tribe in any oil or gas or in the proceeds produced from land subject to the supervision of the United States; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-14(7)(d): oil or gas used in producing or drilling operations or for repressuring or recycling purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-15 Division created -- Functions -- Director of division -- Qualifications of program administrators.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
There is created within the Department of Natural Resources the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining.  The division shall implement the policies and orders of the board and perform all other duties delegated by the board.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16 Duties of division.
-------------------------------------------------
In addition to the duties assigned by the board, the division shall:Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(1): develop and implement an inspection program that will include but not be limited to production data, pre-drilling checks, and site security reviews;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(2): publish a monthly production report;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(3): publish a monthly gas processing plant report;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(4): review and evaluate, prior to a hearing, evidence submitted with the petition to be presented to the board;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(5): 40-6-5 require adequate assurance of approved water rights in accordance with rules and orders enacted under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(6): notify the county executive of the county in which the drilling will take place in writing of the issuance of a drilling permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(7): 59-5-102 complete the verification of natural gas to hydrogen conversion plants required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-16(8): 40-6-24 issue tax credit certificates in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-17 Cooperative research and development projects.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The board and the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining are authorized to enter into cooperative agreements with the national, state or local governments, and with independent organizations and institutions for the purpose of carrying out research and development experiments involving energy resources to the extent that the project is funded or partially funded and approved by the Legislature.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-18 Lands subject to chapter.
-------------------------------------------------------
This act shall apply to all lands in the State of Utah, lawfully subject to its police power, and shall apply to lands of the United States or the lands subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19 Bond and Surety Forfeiture Fund -- Contents -- Use of fund money.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(1): There is created an administrative fund within the General Fund known as the "Bond and Surety Forfeiture Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(2): Money collected by the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining as a result of bond or surety forfeitures shall be deposited in the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(3): Interest earned on money in the fund shall accrue to the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(4)(a): Money from each forfeited bond or surety, together with interest, shall be used by the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining to accomplish the requisite performance standards under the program to which the forfeited bond or surety corresponds.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-19(4)(b): Any money not used for a project shall be returned to the rightful claimant.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20 Use of surface land by owner or operator.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(1): An owner or operator may:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(1)(a): enter onto surface land under which the owner or operator holds rights to conduct oil and gas operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(1)(b): use the surface land:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(1)(b)(i): to the extent reasonably necessary to conduct oil and gas operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(1)(b)(ii): consistent with allowing the surface land owner the greatest possible use of the surface land owner's property, to the extent that the surface land owner's use does not interfere with the owner's or operator's oil and gas operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2): (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(a): mitigate the effects of accessing the surface land owner's surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(b): minimize interference with the surface land owner's use of the surface land owner's property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(c): compensate a surface land owner for unreasonable:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(c)(i): loss of a surface land owner's crops on the surface land;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(c)(ii): loss of value to existing improvements owned by a surface land owner on the surface land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(2)(c)(iii): permanent damage to the surface land.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3): An owner or operator is not required to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3)(a): obtain location or spacing exceptions from the division or board; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3)(b): utilize directional or horizontal drilling techniques that are not:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3)(b)(i): technologically feasible;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3)(b)(ii): economically practicable; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(3)(b)(iii): reasonably available.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(4): (2) The requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5): (5)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a): The provisions of this section do not prevent:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a)(i): a person from seeking a remedy allowed by law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a)(ii): an owner or operator and a surface land owner from addressing the use of surface land for oil and gas operations through:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a)(ii)(A): a lease;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a)(ii)(B): a surface use agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(a)(ii)(C): another written contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(b): (5)(a)(ii) An agreement described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(b)(i): the use of surface land for oil and gas operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20(5)(b)(ii): compensation for damage to the surface land caused by oil and gas operations.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20.5 Title to pore space.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20.5(1): Title to pore space underlying the surface estate is vested in the owner of the surface estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-6-20.5(2): Nothing in this section shall be interpreted to increase or diminish any property right established under the laws of the state.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 7 - Oil and Gas Compact
****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-7-1 Interstate compact to conserve oil and gas -- Authority for governor to join.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The governor of the state of Utah is authorized and directed, for and in the name of the state of Utah to join with the other states in the Interstate Oil Compact to Conserve Oil and Gas, which was executed in Dallas, Texas, on the 16th day of February, 1935, and has been extended to the 1st day of September, 1959, with the consent of Congress, and that said compact and all extensions are now on deposit with the department of state of the United States.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-7-2 Authority for governor to execute extensions or withdraw from compact.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The governor of the state of Utah is authorized and empowered, for and in the name of the state of Utah to execute agreements for further extension of the expiration date of said compact to conserve oil and gas, and to determine if and when it shall be to the best interest of the state of Utah to withdraw from said compact upon 60 days' notice as provided by its terms. In the event that he shall determine that the state shall withdraw from said compact he shall have the power and authority to give necessary notice and to take any and all steps necessary and proper to effect the withdrawal of the state of Utah from said compact.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-7-3 Official representative -- Assistant representative.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The governor shall be the official representative of the state of Utah on the "Interstate Oil Compact Commission" provided for in the compact to conserve oil and gas, and shall exercise and perform for the state all of the powers and duties as members of the Interstate Oil Compact Commission; provided, however, that he shall have the authority to appoint an assistant representative who shall act in his stead as the official representative of the state of Utah as a member of said commission.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 8 - Utah Mined Land Reclamation Act
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-1 Short title.
-----------------------------------------
This act shall be known and may be cited as the "Utah Mined Land Reclamation Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-2 Legislative findings.
--------------------------------------------------
The Utah Legislature finds that:Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-2(1): A mining industry is essential to the economic and physical well-being of the state of Utah and the nation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-2(2): It is necessary to alter the surface of the earth to extract minerals required by our society, but this should be done in such a way as to minimize undesirable effects on the surroundings.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-2(3): Mined land should be reclaimed so as to prevent conditions detrimental to the general safety and welfare of the citizens of the state and to provide for the subsequent use of the lands affected. Reclamation requirements must be adapted to the diversity of topographic, chemical, climatic, biologic, geologic, economic, and social conditions in the areas where mining takes place.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-3 Purpose.
-------------------------------------
The purpose of this act is to provide that from the effective date of the act, except as otherwise provided in this act, all mining in the state shall include plans for reclamation of the land affected.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4 Definitions.
-----------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(1): (1)(a) "Adjudicative proceeding" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(1)(a): a division or board action or proceeding determining the legal rights, duties, privileges, immunities, or other legal interests of one or more identifiable persons, including actions to grant, deny, revoke, suspend, modify, annul, withdraw, or amend an authority, right, permit, or license; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(1)(b): (1)(a) judicial review of a division or board action or proceeding specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(2): "Applicant" means a person who has filed a notice of intent to commence mining operations, or who has applied to the board for a review of a notice or order.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(7): "Conference" means an informal adjudicative proceeding conducted by the division or board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(8): Chapter 6, Board and Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(8)(a): "Deposit" or "mineral deposit" means an accumulation of mineral matter in the form of consolidated rock, unconsolidated material, solutions, or occurring on the surface, beneath the surface, or in the waters of the land from which any product useful to man may be produced, extracted, or obtained or which is extracted by underground mining methods for underground storage.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(8)(b): Chapter 6, Board and Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining "Deposit" or "mineral deposit" excludes sand, gravel, rock aggregate, basalt, boulders, water, geothermal steam, and oil and gas as defined in

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(10): "Division" means the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(12)(a)(i): discovering a deposit or mineral deposit;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(12)(a)(ii): delineating the boundaries of a deposit or mineral deposit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(12)(a)(iii): identifying regions or specific areas in which deposits or mineral deposits are most likely to exist.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(12)(b): (12) "Exploration" includes:

Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(13): "Gravel" means a naturally occurring unconsolidated to moderately consolidated accumulation of rock and mineral particles, the dominant size range being between 4 millimeters and 75 millimeters, that has been deposited by sedimentary processes.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(14): "Hearing" means a formal adjudicative proceeding conducted by the board under the board's procedural rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(15)(a): "Imminent danger to the health and safety of the public" means the existence of a condition or practice, or a violation of a permit requirement or other requirement of this chapter in a mining operation, which condition, practice, or violation could reasonably be expected to cause substantial physical harm to persons outside the permit area before the condition, practice, or violation can be abated.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(15)(b): A reasonable expectation of death or serious injury before abatement exists if a rational person, subjected to the same conditions or practices giving rise to the peril, would not expose the rational person to the danger during the time necessary for abatement.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-8-4(16): (16)
