Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18 Underground coal mining -- Rules regarding surface effects -- Operator requirements -- Repair or compensation for damage -- Replacement of water.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(1): The board shall adopt rules directed toward the surface effects of underground coal mining operations that incorporate the requirements provided in this section.  In adopting any rules, the board shall consider the distinct difference between surface coal mining and underground coal mining methods.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(2): Each permit relating to underground coal mining issued pursuant to this chapter shall require the operator to comply with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3)(a): Except in those instances where the mining technology used requires planned subsidence in a predictable and controlled manner, the operator shall adopt measures consistent with known technology to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3)(a)(i): prevent subsidence from causing material damage, to the extent technologically and economically feasible;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3)(a)(ii): maximize mine stability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3)(a)(iii): maintain the value and reasonably foreseeable use of the surface lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(3)(b): (3)(a) Nothing in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(4): The operator shall seal all portals, entryways, drifts, shafts, or other openings between the surface and underground mine working when no longer needed for the conduct of the mining operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(5): The operator shall fill or seal exploratory holes no longer necessary for mining, maximizing to the extent technologically and economically feasible, the return of mine and processing waste, tailings, and any other waste incident to the mining operation, to the mine workings or excavations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(6)(a): With respect to surface disposal of mine wastes, tailings, coal processing wastes, and other wastes in areas other than the mine workings or excavations, the operator shall stabilize all waste piles created from current operations through construction in compacted layers, including the use of incombustible and impervious materials, if necessary.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(6)(b)(iii): the site is stabilized and revegetated according to the provisions of this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18(10): The operator shall eliminate fire hazards and other conditions which constitute a hazard to health and safety of the public.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18.1 Suspension of underground mining upon finding of immediate danger to inhabitants at surface.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
In order to protect the stability of the land, the board shall suspend underground coal mining under urbanized areas, cities, towns, and communities and adjacent to industrial or commercial buildings, major impoundments, or permanent streams if, after proper notice and hearing, there is a finding of imminent danger to inhabitants of the urbanized areas, cities, towns, and communities.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-18.2 Applicability of other chapter provisions.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
The provisions of this chapter relating to permits, sureties, bonds, inspections, and enforcement, public review, and administrative and judicial review shall be applicable to surface operations and surface impacts incident to an underground coal mine with those modifications to the permit application requirements, permit approval or denial procedures, and bond requirements as are necessary to accommodate the distinct difference between surface and underground coal mining methods.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19 Information provided by permittees to division -- Inspections by division -- Signs required at operations entrances -- Violations reported by reclamation officers -- Copies of records and reports available to public.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(1): For the purpose of developing, administering, and enforcing any permit under this chapter, or of determining whether any person is in violation of any requirement of this chapter, the division shall require any permittee to provide information relative to surface coal mining and reclamation operations as the division deems reasonable and necessary in the division's rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(2): (2); 40-8-17(2) The authorized representatives of the division, without advance notice and upon presentation of appropriate credentials:

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(3): The inspections by the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(3)(a): occur on an irregular basis averaging not less than one partial inspection per month and one complete inspection per calendar quarter for the surface coal mining and reclamation operation covered by each permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(3)(b): occur without prior notice to the permittee or his agents or employees except for necessary onsite meetings with the permittee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(3)(c): include the filing of inspection reports adequate to enforce the requirements of and to carry out the terms and purposes of this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-19(6): Copies of any records, reports, inspection materials, or information obtained under this chapter by the division shall be made immediately available to the public.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20 Civil penalty for violation of chapter -- Informal conference -- Public hearing -- Contest of violation or amount of penalty -- Collection -- Criminal penalties -- Civil penalty for failure to correct violation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1): 40-10-22
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(a): 40-10-22 Any permittee who violates any permit condition or other provision of this chapter may be assessed a civil penalty by the division.  If the violation leads to the issuance of a cessation order under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(b)(i): The penalty may not exceed $5,000 for each violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(b)(ii): Each day of a continuing violation may be deemed a separate violation for purposes of the penalty assessments.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(c): In determining the amount of the penalty, consideration shall be given to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(c)(i): the permittee's history of previous violations at the particular surface coal mining operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(c)(ii): the seriousness of the violation, including any irreparable harm to the environment and any hazard to the health or safety of the public;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(c)(iii): whether the permittee was negligent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(1)(c)(iv): the demonstrated good faith of the permittee in attempting to achieve rapid compliance after notification of the violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(a): Within 30 days after the issuance of a notice or order charging that a violation of this chapter has occurred, the division shall inform the permittee of the proposed assessment.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(b): The person charged with the penalty shall then have 30 days to pay the proposed assessment in full, or request an informal conference before the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(c): The informal conference held by the division may address either the amount of the proposed assessment or the fact of the violation, or both.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(d): If the permittee who requested the informal conference and participated in the proceedings is not in agreement with the results of the informal conference, the permittee may, within 30 days of receipt of the decision made by the division in the informal conference, request a hearing before the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(e)(i): Prior to any review of the proposed assessment or the fact of a violation by the board, and within 30 days of receipt of the decision made by the division in the informal conference, the permittee shall forward to the division the amount of the proposed assessment for placement in an escrow account.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(e)(ii): If the operator fails to forward the amount of the penalty to the division within 30 days of receipt of the results of the informal conference, the operator waives any opportunity for further review of the fact of the violation or to contest the amount of the civil penalty assessed for the violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(2)(e)(iii): If, through administrative or judicial review, it is determined that no violation occurred or that the amount of the penalty should be reduced, the division shall within 30 days remit the appropriate amount to the operator with interest accumulated.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-20(3): (1); 40-10-22

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22 Violation of chapter or permit conditions -- Inspection -- Cessation order, abatement notice, or show cause order -- Suspension or revocation of permit -- Review -- Costs assessed against either party.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1): (1)(e); (1)(e)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1)(a): Whenever, on the basis of any information available, including receipt of information from any person, the division has reason to believe that any person is in violation of any requirement of this chapter or any permit condition required by this chapter, the division shall immediately order inspection of the surface coal mining operation at which the alleged violation is occurring, unless the information available to the division is a result of a previous inspection of the surface coal mining operation.  When the inspection results from information provided to the division by any person, the division shall notify that person when the inspection is proposed to be carried out, and that person shall be allowed to accompany the inspector during the inspection.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1)(b): (1)(e) When, on the basis of any inspection, the division determines that any condition or practices exist, or that any permittee is in violation of any requirement of this chapter or any permit condition required by this chapter, which condition, practice, or violation also creates an imminent danger to the health or safety of the public, or is causing, or can reasonably be expected to cause significant, imminent environmental harm to land, air, or water resources, the division shall immediately order a cessation of surface coal mining and reclamation operations or the portion thereof relevant to the condition, practice, or violation.  The cessation order shall remain in effect until the division determines that the condition, practice, or violation has been abated, or until modified, vacated, or terminated by the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1)(c): (1)(e) When, on the basis of an inspection, the division determines that any permittee is in violation of any requirement of this chapter or any permit condition required by this chapter, but the violation does not create an imminent danger to the health or safety of the public or cannot be reasonably expected to cause significant, imminent environmental harm to land, air, or water resources, the division shall issue a notice to the permittee or his agent fixing a reasonable time but not more than 90 days for the abatement of the violation and providing opportunity for conference before the division.  If upon expiration of the period of time as originally fixed or subsequently extended, for good cause shown, and upon the written finding of the division, the division finds that the violation has not been abated, it shall immediately order a cessation of surface coal mining and reclamation operations or the portion of same relevant to the violation.  The cessation order shall remain in effect until the division determines that the violation has been abated or until modified, vacated, or terminated by the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1)(d): When on the basis of an inspection the division determines that a pattern of violations of any requirements of this chapter or any permit conditions required by this chapter exists or has existed, and if the division also finds that these violations are caused by the unwarranted failure of the permittee to comply with any requirements of this chapter or any permit conditions or that these violations are willfully caused by the permittee, the division shall initiate agency action by requesting the board to issue an order to show cause to the permittee as to why the permit should not be suspended or revoked and shall provide opportunity for a public hearing.  If a hearing is requested, the board shall give notice in accordance with the rules of practice and procedure of the board.  Upon the permittee's failure to show cause as to why the permit should not be suspended or revoked, the board shall immediately enter an order to suspend or revoke the permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-22(1)(e): Notices and orders issued under this section shall set forth with reasonable specificity the nature of the violation and the remedial action required, the period of time established for abatement, and a reasonable description of the portion of the surface coal mining and reclamation operation to which the notice or order applies.  Each notice or order issued under this section shall be given promptly to the permittee or his agent by the division, and the notices and orders shall be in writing and shall be signed by the director, or his authorized representative who issues such notice or order.  Any notice or order issued under this section may be modified, vacated, or terminated by the division, but any notice or order issued under this section which requires cessation of mining by the operator shall expire within 30 days of actual notice to the operator unless a conference is held before the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-23 Time for bringing criminal proceeding.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
No criminal proceeding based upon violation of this chapter, or any rule, regulation, or order issued under this chapter, shall be commenced or maintained unless it shall have been commenced within five years from the date of the alleged violation.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(1)(b): (2) Upon petition pursuant to Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(1)(c)(i)(B): affect fragile or historic lands in which the operations could result in significant damage to important historic, cultural, scientific, and aesthetic values and natural systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(1)(c)(i)(C): affect renewable resource lands in which the operations could result in a substantial loss or reduction of long-range productivity of water supply or of food or fiber products, and the lands to include aquifers and aquifer recharge areas; or

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(2)(a): Any person having an interest which is or may be adversely affected shall have the right to petition the board to have an area designated as unsuitable for surface coal mining operations or to have this designation terminated.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(2)(b): The petition shall contain allegations of facts with supporting evidence which would tend to establish the allegations.  Within 10 months after receipt of the petition the board shall hold a public hearing, after appropriate notice and publication of the date, time, and location of the hearing.  After a person having an interest which is or may be adversely affected has filed a petition and before the hearing, as required by this subsection, any person may intervene by filing allegations of facts with supporting evidence which would tend to establish the allegations.  Within 60 days after the hearing, the board shall issue and furnish to the petitioner and any other party to the hearing, a written decision regarding the petition and the reasons for it.  If all the petitioners stipulate agreement prior to the requested hearing and withdraw their request, the hearing need not be held.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(3): Prior to any land areas being designated as unsuitable for surface coal mining operations, a detailed statement shall be prepared by the division on:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(3)(a): the potential coal resources of the area;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(3)(b): the demand for coal resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(3)(c): the impact of the designation on the environment, the economy, and the supply of coal.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(4): After August 3, 1977, and subject to valid existing rights, no surface coal mining operations, except those which exist on that date, shall be permitted:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(4)(a): on any lands where this activity is precluded by Public Law 95-87;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(4)(b): on any lands which will adversely affect any publicly owned park or places included in the National Register of Historic Sites, unless approved jointly by the division and the federal, state, or local agency with jurisdiction over the park or the historic site;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(4)(c): within 100 feet of the outside right-of-way line of any public road, except where mine access roads or haulage roads join this right-of-way line and except that the division may permit these roads to be relocated or the area affected to lie within 100 feet of the road, if after public notice and opportunity for public hearing in the locality a written finding is made that the interests of the public and the landowners affected thereby will be protected; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-24(4)(d): within 300 feet from any occupied dwelling, unless waived by the owner of same, nor within 300 feet from any public building, school, church, community, institutional building, or public park, or within 100 feet of a cemetery.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-25.2(1): The state is not liable for any costs or damages resulting from action taken or not taken to carry out an abandoned mine reclamation plan.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26 State reclamation plan and annual projects submitted to Secretary of Interior -- Contents of plan -- Annual support and implementation requests -- Costs for proposed projects.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26(1): The division will submit to the Secretary of the Interior a state reclamation plan and annual projects to carry out the purposes of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26(2): The state reclamation plan shall generally identify the areas to be reclaimed, the purposes for which the reclamation is proposed, the relationship of the lands to be reclaimed and the proposed reclamation to surrounding areas, the specific criteria for ranking and identifying projects to be funded, and the legal authority and programmatic capability to perform this work in conformance with the provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26(3): The division shall have the authority to submit an annual application for the support of the state program and implementation of specific reclamation projects to the Secretary of the Interior. These annual requests shall include such information as may be requested by the Secretary.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26(4): (3) The division shall have the authority to provide annual and other reports required by the Secretary of the Interior to accompany the annual request for support required in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-26(5): The costs for each proposed project under this section shall include: actual construction costs, actual operation and maintenance costs of permanent facilities, planning and engineering costs, construction inspection costs, and other necessary administrative expenses.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(2)(a): The agents, employees, or contractors of the division may enter upon any property for the purpose of conducting studies or exploratory work to determine the existence of adverse effects of past coal mining practices and to determine the feasibility of restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of these adverse effects.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(2)(b): This entry shall be construed as an exercise of the police power for the protection of public health, safety, and general welfare and may not be construed as an act of condemnation of property or trespass on it.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(3): The state may acquire any land by purchase, donation, or condemnation which is adversely affected by past coal mining practices if the board, after notice and hearing, determines that acquisition of this land is necessary to successful reclamation and that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(3)(a): the acquired land, after restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of the adverse effects of past coal mining practices, will serve recreation and historic purposes, conservation and reclamation purposes, or provide open space benefits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(3)(b)(i): permanent facilities such as a treatment plant or a relocated stream channel will be constructed on the land for the restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of the adverse effects of past coal mining practices; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(3)(b)(ii): acquisitions of coal refuse disposal sites and all coal refuse on the sites will serve the purposes of this chapter or that public ownership is desirable to meet emergency situations and prevent recurrences of the adverse effects of past coal mining practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(4)(a): Title to all lands acquired under this section shall be in the name of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(4)(b): The price paid for land acquired under this section shall reflect the market value of the land as adversely affected by past coal mining practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(5)(a): If land acquired under this section is considered suitable for industrial, commercial, residential, or recreational development, the division, in conjunction with the Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands, may sell this land by public sale under a system of competitive bidding, at not less than fair market value, and under any other rules promulgated to insure that the land is put to proper use consistent with local and state land use plans.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(5)(b)(i): The state, when requested after appropriate public notice, shall hold a public hearing with the appropriate notice, in the counties or appropriate political subdivisions of the state in which lands acquired under this section are located.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(5)(b)(ii): The hearing shall be held at a time which shall afford local citizens and governments the maximum opportunity to participate in the decision concerning the use or disposition of the lands after restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of the adverse effects of past coal mining practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(6)(a): The state, through the division and the Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands, shall have the authority to accept lands acquired and reclaimed by the Secretary of the Interior pursuant to Section 407(h) of Public Law 95-87.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(6)(b): The division has the authority to accept grants from the Secretary to carry out the purposes of Section 407(h) of Public Law 95-87.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(7)(a): Within six months after the completion of projects to restore, reclaim, abate, control, or prevent adverse effects of past coal mining practices on privately owned land, the division shall itemize the money expended and may file a statement of those expenses in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the land lies, together with a notarized appraisal by an independent appraiser of the value of the land before the restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of adverse effects of past coal mining practices if the money expended results in a significant increase in property value.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(7)(b): This statement shall constitute a lien upon the land described in it.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(7)(c): The lien may not exceed the amount determined by the appraisal to be the increase in the market value of the land as a result of the restoration, reclamation, abatement, control, or prevention of the adverse effects of past coal mining practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(7)(d): A lien may not be filed against the property of any person, in accordance with this subsection, who owned the surface prior to May 2, 1977, and who neither consented to nor participated in nor exercised control over the mining operation which necessitated the reclamation performed.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-27(9)(b): The statement shall constitute a lien upon the land as of the date of the expenditure of the money and shall have priority as a lien second only to the lien of real estate taxes imposed upon the land.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28 Recovery of reclamation costs -- Lien against reclaimed land.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1): All reclamation costs of each project shall be recovered to the extent possible, taking into consideration the objectives of the project and the criteria under which the project was selected for reclamation work, in accordance with the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(a): All possible reclamation costs shall be recovered at the time of first sale of land following reclamation as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(a)(i): Whenever reclaimed land is sold at a value higher than that at which the unreclaimed land was appraised immediately prior to reclamation, the difference between the pre and post reclamation values shall be payable to the fund to mitigate or offset the cost of the reclamation program.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(a)(ii): When land is to be sold to a state or local government for public purposes, the amount of the sale price may be less than the market value after reclamation but may not be less than the actual cost of the purchase of the property by the state plus the costs of reclamation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(b)(i): Special charges for use of land may be levied, including recreation fees, leases, livestock grazing fees, or other land use fees. These fees may be waived by the division when deemed to be to the public benefit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(b)(ii): These user fees, however, shall be charged to all users of the reclaimed lands if the uses result in financial or personal benefits to persons, corporations, or profit-making organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(1)(b)(iii): All fees collected, less operating and maintenance expenses, shall be deposited in the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(2)(a): The division shall place a lien against reclaimed land, the market value of which has increased as a result of the reclamation work, except where the surface owner owned the land prior to May 2, 1977, and neither consented to nor participated in nor exercised control over the mining operation which necessitated the reclamation work.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(2)(b): The division may waive the requirement of a lien where land is owned by a state, local government, or municipality or when owned and operated for a charitable public purpose by a nonprofit charitable organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(2)(c): The amount of the lien shall consist of the money expended for the reclamation work but shall not exceed the resulting increase in the market value of the reclaimed land as determined by an independent appraiser.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-28(2)(d): A written statement of money expended for the reclamation work, together with a notarized appraisal of an independent appraiser of the market value of the land before and after the reclamation work, shall within six months after completion of the reclamation work, be filed in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the land lies.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-29 Other enforcement and protection rights unaffected -- Operator to replace adversely affected water supply of legitimate users.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-29(1): Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as affecting in any way the right of any person to enforce or protect, under applicable law, his interest in water resources affected by a surface coal mining operation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-29(2): The operator of a surface coal mine shall replace the water supply of an owner of interest in real property who obtains all or part of his supply of water for domestic, agricultural, industrial, or other legitimate use from an underground or surface source where this supply has been affected by contamination, diminution, or interruption proximately resulting from the surface coal mine operation.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30 Judicial review of rules or orders.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Judicial review of adjudicative proceedings under this chapter is governed by
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Judicial review of the board's rulemaking procedures and rules adopted under this chapter is governed by
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3): An appeal from an order of the board shall be directly to the Utah Supreme Court and is not a trial de novo.  The court shall set aside the board action if it is found to be:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(a): unreasonable, unjust, arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(b): contrary to constitutional right, power, privilege, or immunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(c): in excess of statutory jurisdiction, authority, or limitations;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(d): not in compliance with procedure required by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(e): based upon a clearly erroneous interpretation or application of the law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(3)(f): as to an adjudicative proceeding, unsupported by substantial evidence on the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(4): 78A-3-102 An action or appeal involving an order of the board shall be determined as expeditiously as feasible and in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-10-30(5): If the board fails to perform any act or duty under this chapter which is not discretionary, the aggrieved person may bring an action in the district court of the county in which the operation or proposed operation is located.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 40 - Chapter 11 - Geologic Carbon Storage
*********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(1): "Board" means the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(2): 19-6-102
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(2)(a): "Carbon dioxide" means carbon dioxide (CO2) that has been captured from an emission source or direct air capture, plus incidental associated substances derived from the source materials and the capture process, and any substances added to the carbon dioxide to enable or improve the injection process.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(2)(b): 19-6-102 "Carbon dioxide" does not include hazardous waste as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(3): "Class VI injection well" means the same as that term is defined in 40 C.F.R. 146.5(f).
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(4): "Division" means the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(5): "Geologic carbon storage" means the permanent or short-term underground storage of carbon dioxide in a storage reservoir.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6): Title 40, Chapter 11, Geologic Carbon Storage "Geologic carbon storage activity" means activity associated with the development, production, processing, and storage of carbon dioxide as set forth in
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(a): drilling;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(b): development of storage facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(c): completion, maintenance, reworking, recompletion, disposal, plugging, and abandonment of storage facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(d): construction activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(e): recovery techniques;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(f): remediation activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(6)(g): any other activity related to geologic carbon storage that the board identifies.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(7): "Permit" means a permit issued by the division and approved by the board allowing a person to operate a storage facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(8): "Reservoir" means a subsurface sedimentary stratum, formation, aquifer, cavity, or void, whether natural or artificially created, including oil and gas reservoirs, saline formations, and coal seams suitable for or capable of being made suitable for geologic carbon storage.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(9)(a): "Storage facility" means the reservoir, underground equipment, and surface facilities and equipment used or proposed to be used in a geologic carbon storage operation.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(9)(b): "Storage facility" does not include pipelines used to transport carbon dioxide to a storage facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-1(10): "Storage operator" means a person holding or applying for a permit.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2 Preemption.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(1): Regulation of geologic carbon storage is of statewide concern and the state regulation of geologic carbon storage activity occupies the whole field of geologic carbon storage subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(1)(a): the granting of primacy over Class VI geologic sequestration wells; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(1)(b): relevant federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(2): The legislative body of a political subdivision may enact, amend, or enforce a local ordinance, resolution, or rule consistent with the political subdivision's general land use authority that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(2)(a): regulates only surface activity that is incidental to geologic carbon storage activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(2)(b): does not effectively or unduly limit, ban, or prohibit geologic carbon storage activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-2(2)(c): is not otherwise preempted by state or federal law.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3 Board authority -- Rulemaking authority.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(1): The board and the division have jurisdiction over all persons and property necessary to enforce this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act To enforce this chapter, the board shall make rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(3): Subject to the granting of primacy by the Environmental Protection Agency under the process required in 40 C.F.R. Section 145 and successful application for primacy approval under Section 1425 of the Safe Drinking Water Act, the board and the division have:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(3)(a): exclusive jurisdiction in the state over Class VI injection wells located in the state on nonfederal lands; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(3)(b): cooperative jurisdiction in the state over Class VI injection wells located in the state on federal lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(4): 63J-1-504 The board shall establish fees in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(4)(a): the permitting process;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(4)(b): the regulation of the construction, operation, and pre-closure activities of the storage facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-3(4)(c): the monitoring of closed storage facilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4 Board and division permit authority.
------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent required to authorize and issue permits and to regulate geologic carbon sequestration, the board and the division shall have authority:Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(1): over all persons and property necessary to administer and enforce this chapter and this chapter's objectives;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(2): to regulate activities relating to a storage facility, including construction, operation, and closure;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(3): to enter, at a reasonable time and manner, a storage facility to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(3)(a): inspect equipment and surface storage facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(3)(b): observe, monitor, and investigate operations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(3)(c): inspect records the board requires the operators maintain at the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(4): to require that storage operators provide assurance, including bonds, that money is available to fulfill the storage operator's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(5): to exercise continuing jurisdiction over storage operators and storage facilities, including the authority, after notice and hearing, to amend provisions in a permit and to revoke a permit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-4(6): to dissolve or change the boundaries of any unit that is within or near a storage reservoir's boundaries.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-5 Permits.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-5(1): 40-11-3 Subject to the granting of primacy as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-5(2): A person may only transfer a permit to another person with permission of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-5(3): A person may not engage in geologic carbon storage in the state without a permit.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6 Permit application requirements.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(1): A person applying for a permit shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(1)(a): comply with:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(1)(a)(i): the application requirements the board establishes through rule; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(1)(a)(ii): the application requirements described in this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(1)(b): pay a fee, as established by the board, to cover the administrative costs of considering an application for a permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(2): The board shall give priority to storage operators who apply for a permit to store carbon dioxide produced in Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3): 40-11-13 A permit application shall demonstrate:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(a): that the storage operator has complied with all requirements established by the board in rule and in this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(b): that the storage facility is suitable for carbon dioxide injection and storage;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(c): that the carbon dioxide the storage operator will store is of a quality that allows the carbon dioxide to be safely and efficiently stored in the reservoir;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(d): that the storage operator has made a good-faith effort to get the consent of all persons who own the storage reservoir's pore space;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(e): that owners who own no less than 70% of the reservoir's pore space have provided written consent to the use of the owners' pore space for a storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(f): whether the storage facility contains commercially valuable minerals;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(g): if the storage facility contains commercially valuable minerals:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(g)(i): a plan for addressing the ownership interests of the mineral owners or mineral lessees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(g)(ii): a demonstration that the storage facility will not negatively impact the commercially valuable minerals;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(h): 40-11-13 that the storage reservoir meets the integrity requirements described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i): that the operator has taken reasonable steps to ensure that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(i): the storage facility will not endanger human health;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(ii): the storage facility will not endanger the environment;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(iii): the storage facility is in the public interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(iv): the storage facility will not adversely affect surface water or formation containing fresh water;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(v): carbon dioxide will not escape from the storage reservoir at a rate exceeding the lower of 1% or the standard recommended by the Environmental Protection Agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(i)(vi): that substances that compromise the objectives of this chapter or the integrity of a reservoir will not enter the reservoir;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(j): that the storage reservoir has defined horizontal and vertical boundaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(k): that the boundaries of the storage reservoir include buffer areas to ensure the safe operation of the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(l): plans for monitoring the storage facility and procedures to assess the location and migration of carbon dioxide injected for storage;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(m): plans to ensure compliance with geologic carbon storage statutes and rules; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-6(3)(n): assurance that all nonconsenting pore space owners are or will be equitably compensated for the use of the pore space of the nonconsenting pore space owners in the storage facility.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10 Amalgamation of interests -- Board may order amalgamation -- Payment of costs and interests -- Accounting.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(1): Two or more owners of contiguous pore space may bring together the owners' interests for the development of a storage facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(a): In the absence of a written agreement for amalgamation, including a joint operating agreement, the board may enter an order combining all interests in the contiguous pore space for the development of a storage facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(b): The order shall be made upon terms and conditions that are just and reasonable.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(c): The board may adopt terms appearing in a joint operating agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(c)(i): for the storage facility that is in effect between the consenting owners;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(c)(ii): submitted by any party to the proceeding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(2)(c)(iii): submitted by the board on the board's own motion.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(3): Operations incident to the construction or operation of a storage facility upon any portion of an area included in an amalgamation order shall be deemed for all purposes to be the conduct of the operations upon each separately owned tract in the area by the several orders.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4): (4)(d); (4)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a)(i): Each amalgamation order shall provide for the payment of just and reasonable costs incurred in the construction and operation of the storage facility, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a)(i)(A): the costs of constructing, marketing, completing, and operating the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a)(i)(B): reasonable charges for the administration and supervision of operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a)(i)(C): other costs customarily incurred in the industry.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(a)(ii): An owner is not liable under an amalgamation order for costs or losses resulting from the gross negligence or willful misconduct of the operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(b): Each amalgamation order shall provide for reimbursement to the consenting owners for any nonconsenting owner's share of the costs of operation of the storage facility attributable to the nonconsenting owner's tract.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(c): (4)(d) Each amalgamation order shall provide that each consenting owner shall own and be entitled to receive, subject to taxes, fees, fines, and other obligations:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(c)(i): the share of the profits of the storage facility applicable to the consenting owner's interest in the storage facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(c)(ii): (4)(d) unless the consenting owner has agreed otherwise, the consenting owner's proportionate part of the nonconsenting owner's share of the profits until the recovery of costs provided for in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d): (4)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(i): Each amalgamation order shall provide that each nonconsenting owner shall be entitled to receive, subject to obligations, the share of the profits from the storage facility applicable to the nonconsenting owner's interest in the storage facility after the consenting owners have recovered from the nonconsenting owner's share of the profits the following amounts less any cash contributions the nonconsenting owner has made:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(i)(A): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the cost of storage facility construction and maintenance;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(i)(B): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the estimated cost to close the storage facility as the board determines;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(i)(C): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the cost of operation of the storage facility commencing with the first injection of carbon dioxide and continuing until the consenting owners have recovered all costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(i)(D): 100% of the nonconsenting owner's share of the costs of preparing the storage facility, rights-of-way, and equipment.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(ii): (4)(d)(i) The nonconsenting owner's share of the costs specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(d)(iii): The board may include a reasonable interest charge if the board finds it appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(4)(e): The board shall determine the proper costs to resolve any dispute about costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(5): The operator of a storage facility under an amalgamation order in which there is a nonconsenting owner shall furnish the nonconsenting owner with monthly statements specifying:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(5)(a): costs incurred; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(5)(b): profit realized.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6): (4)(d) Each amalgamation order shall provide that when the consenting owners recover from a nonconsenting owner's relinquished interest the amounts provided for in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6)(a): the relinquished interest of the nonconsenting owner shall automatically revert to the nonconsenting owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6)(b): the nonconsenting owner shall from that time:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6)(b)(i): own the same interest in the storage facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6)(b)(ii): be liable for the further costs of the operation as if the nonconsenting owner had participated in the initial drilling and operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(6)(b)(iii): costs are payable out of profits unless otherwise agreed between the nonconsenting owner and the operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(7): Each amalgamation order shall provide that in any circumstance where the nonconsenting owner has relinquished the nonconsenting owner's share of profits to consenting owners or at any time fails to take the nonconsenting owner's share of benefits when the nonconsenting owner is entitled to do so, the nonconsenting owner is entitled to:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(7)(a): an accounting of the profits applicable to the nonconsenting owner's relinquished share of the storage facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(7)(b): payment of the profits applicable to that share of the profits not taken in-kind, net of costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-10(8): (4)(d) A nonconsenting owner who does not take the nonconsenting owner's share of the profits is not liable for the costs described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11 Geologic carbon storage amalgamation unit -- Procedure for establishment -- Operation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(1): The board may hold a hearing to consider the need for the amalgamation of a tract for geologic carbon storage.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(2): The board shall make an order providing for the amalgamation of a tract for geologic carbon storage, if the board finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(2)(a): amalgamation is reasonably necessary for the purposes of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(2)(b): the value of amalgamation justifies proceeding against the nonconsenting owner's wishes.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3): The amalgamation order shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(a): a description of the lands and of the reservoir to become a storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(b): a statement of the nature of the operations contemplated;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(c): an allocation to the separately owned tracts in the amalgamation unit of the profits the storage facility receives, considering:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(c)(i): agreements among interested parties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(c)(ii): the relative value of the separately owned tracts within the amalgamation area;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(d): a provision for adjustment among the owners of the amalgamation area for investments made prior to the amalgamation order;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(e): a provision determining the allocation of costs among owners, and how the owners shall pay those costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(f): any necessary provision for:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(f)(i): financing an owner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(f)(ii): carrying an owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(g): a provision for the supervision and conduct of the storage facility operations, including a percentage vote for each owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(h): additional provisions that are necessary and appropriate for carrying on the operation of the amalgamation unit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(3)(i): the designation of an operator of the amalgamation unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(4): (3) An amalgamation order described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(4)(a): owners whose obligations under the amalgamation order require them to pay not less than 70% of the costs for operating and constructing the facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-11(4)(b): owners whose combined interest under the amalgamation order is not less than 70% of the profits from the operation of the storage facility.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-12 Requirement to record.
-----------------------------------------------------
An operator shall file a record of the permit and a description of the impacted land with the recorder's office in each county where the storage facility is located.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13 Reservoir integrity.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(1): 4-18-103; 4-44-102 Carbon dioxide injected into and stored in a reservoir in compliance with the requirements of this section is not:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(1)(a): 4-18-103 pollution, as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(1)(b): 4-44-102 a nuisance, as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(2): A reservoir is only appropriate for geologic carbon storage if the board determines and the operator demonstrates that:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(2)(a): carbon dioxide cannot escape the reservoir at a rate exceeding the lower of 1% or the standard recommended by the Environmental Protection Agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(2)(b): no additional substances will be introduced into the storage facility that could compromise the integrity of the storage reservoir; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(2)(c): the operator has a plan to maintain the integrity of the reservoir.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(3): (2); 79-3-201; 19-1-104 When making a determination described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(3)(a): 79-3-201 a finding from the Utah Geological Survey, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(3)(b): 19-1-104 reports and findings from the Department of Environmental Quality, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-13(4): The board shall take action to enforce the provisions of this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-14 Preservation of rights.
------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter or in a permit may be interpreted to:Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-14(1): prejudice the rights of property owners who own property that hosts a storage facility to the extent that those property rights are not committed to the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-14(2): prevent a mineral owner or mineral lessee from drilling through or near a storage reservoir to explore or develop mineral resources to the extent that the exploration and development:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-14(2)(a): preserves the integrity of the storage facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-14(2)(b): complies with requirements described in this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-15 Title to injected carbon dioxide.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-15(1): The storage operator has title to the carbon dioxide injected into and stored in a storage reservoir and holds title until the board issues a certificate of project completion.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-15(2): The storage operator is liable for any damage the stored carbon dioxide may cause, including damage caused by escaping stored carbon dioxide until the board issues a certificate of completion.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-15(3): An owner of pore space does not incur liability for geologic carbon storage activity by virtue of ownership of or of leasing out the pore space.


Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16 Certificate of project completion.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1): To request a certificate of project completion, a storage operator shall submit:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(a): a demonstration that the last carbon dioxide injection was no fewer than 10 years preceding the filing;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(b): a statement of compliance with all statutes and rules regulating the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(c): a demonstration of the resolution of all pending claims regarding the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(d): a demonstration of the present and future physical integrity of the storage reservoir;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(e): a demonstration that any carbon dioxide in the storage reservoir:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(e)(i): is essentially stationary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(e)(ii): if the carbon dioxide migrates or will migrate, is highly unlikely to cross the storage reservoir boundary;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(f): a demonstration that all wells, equipment, and facilities necessary for maintaining the continued integrity of the storage reservoir are currently in good condition and will maintain that good condition;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(g): a demonstration that the operator has:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(g)(i): plugged wells;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(g)(ii): removed equipment and facilities not necessary to maintaining the integrity of the reservoir; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(1)(g)(iii): completed any other reclamation work the board requires.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2): Immediately after the board issues a certificate of completion:
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2)(a): title to the storage facility and the stored carbon dioxide transfers to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2)(b): liability with respect to the storage facility and the stored carbon dioxide transfers to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2)(c): the storage operator and any person who is not the state who has property rights in the storage facility is released from any obligation to comply with regulatory requirements associated with the storage facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2)(d): the board shall release any bonds the storage operator has posted; and
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-16(2)(e): the division shall oversee the monitoring and managing of the storage facility.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-17(1): This chapter does not apply to the injection of carbon dioxide for an enhanced oil or gas recovery project.
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-17(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-17(2)(a): This chapter does apply to the conversion of an enhanced oil or gas recovery project to a storage facility.

Utah Code Annotated § 40-11-19 Participation of public interests.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
The governing body of a controlling state interest or interest of a political subdivision is authorized to consent to and participate in a geologic carbon storage project.
